Fed Up With	<b>Bengali:</b> বিরক্ত হয়ে যাওয়া; ধৈর্য হারানো<br><b>English:</b> Refusing to tolerate something any further; out of patience<br><b>Example:</b> I'm fed up with his constant excuses for being late.	
Feel Like a Million Dollars	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব ভাল অনুভব করা<br><b>English:</b> To feel great, to feel well and healthy<br><b>Example:</b> After the spa treatment, she felt like a million dollars.	
Feel On Top of The World	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত সুস্থ বোধ করা<br><b>English:</b> To feel very healthy<br><b>Example:</b> After recovering from illness, he felt on top of the world.	
Fell off a Truck	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্ভবত চোরাই মাল<br><b>English:</b> Probably stolen or illicitly obtained<br><b>Example:</b> Those expensive watches that 'fell off a truck' are clearly stolen goods.	
Fifteen Minutes of Fame	<b>Bengali:</b> অস্থায়ী খ্যাতি<br><b>English:</b> Temporary renown<br><b>Example:</b> The viral video gave him his fifteen minutes of fame.	
Fifth Wheel	<b>Bengali:</b> অপ্রয়োজনীয় ব্যক্তি<br><b>English:</b> A superfluous person<br><b>Example:</b> At the couples' dinner, I felt like a fifth wheel.	
Fight Fire with Fire	<b>Bengali:</b> শত্রুর বিপরীতে সমান শক্তি প্রয়োগ করা<br><b>English:</b> Use the same measures that are being used against you<br><b>Example:</b> If they're spreading rumors about us, we'll fight fire with fire.	
Fight Like Cat and Dog	<b>Bengali:</b> ক্রমাগত ঝগড়া করা<br><b>English:</b> Continually arguing with each other<br><b>Example:</b> The siblings fight like cat and dog but really love each other.	
Find One's Voice	<b>Bengali:</b> নিজেকে প্রকাশে আত্মবিশ্বাসী হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Become more confident in expressing oneself<br><b>Example:</b> After years of shyness, she finally found her voice in college.	
Find Your Feet	<b>Bengali:</b> নতুন পরিস্থিতিতে খাপ খাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To adjust to a new place or situation<br><b>Example:</b> It took him a few months to find his feet in the new job.	
Finger-Pointing	<b>Bengali:</b> দোষারোপ করা<br><b>English:</b> Blame; a situation where each member attempts to blame others<br><b>Example:</b> Stop the finger-pointing and let's focus on solutions.	
Fire in the Belly	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রবল উচ্চাকাঙ্ক্ষা<br><b>English:</b> Strong ambition<br><b>Example:</b> She has the fire in the belly needed to succeed in business.	
First In, Best Dressed	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রথম আসা প্রথম পাওয়ার সুবিধা<br><b>English:</b> The first people to do something will have an advantage<br><b>Example:</b> The concert tickets are first in, best dressed - no reservations.	
Fish for Compliments	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রশংসা আদায়ের চেষ্টা করা<br><b>English:</b> Try to manipulate people into praising you<br><b>Example:</b> Stop fishing for compliments - we all know you did a great job.	
Fish or Cut Bait	<b>Bengali:</b> সিদ্ধান্ত নাও বা অন্যকে সুযোগ দাও<br><b>English:</b> Make a decision or give someone else a chance<br><b>Example:</b> It's time to fish or cut bait - either commit to the project or step aside.	
Fish Out of Water	<b>Bengali:</b> অচেনা পরিবেশে অস্বস্তি বোধকারী<br><b>English:</b> A person who is in unfamiliar, confusing surroundings<br><b>Example:</b> At the fancy gala, the farmer felt like a fish out of water.	
Five-Finger Discount	<b>Bengali:</b> চুরি<br><b>English:</b> Shoplifting<br><b>Example:</b> He got those expensive headphones with a five-finger discount.	
Flash in the Pan	<b>Bengali:</b> ক্ষণস্থায়ী ঘটনা<br><b>English:</b> A one-time occurrence, not a permanent phenomenon<br><b>Example:</b> His success was just a flash in the pan - he never won another race.	
Flat Broke	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্পূর্ণ অর্থহীন<br><b>English:</b> Having no money at all<br><b>Example:</b> After the gambling spree, he was flat broke.	
Flat Out Like a Lizard Drinking	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত ব্যস্ত<br><b>English:</b> Very busy<br><b>Example:</b> I've been flat out like a lizard drinking all week with this project.	
Flesh and Blood	<b>Bengali:</b> রক্তের সম্পর্কের আত্মীয়<br><b>English:</b> Blood relatives, close relatives<br><b>Example:</b> I can't turn my back on him - he's my own flesh and blood.	
Flew the Coop	<b>Bengali:</b> পালিয়ে গেছে<br><b>English:</b> Left, escaped<br><b>Example:</b> When we arrived at the hideout, the criminals had already flown the coop.	
Flip-Flop	<b>Bengali:</b> দ্বিধাদ্বন্দ্বে থাকা<br><b>English:</b> To vacillate between two choices, to be indecisive<br><b>Example:</b> Stop flip-flopping and make a decision about which college to attend.	
Fly by the Seat of One's Pants	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিকল্পনা ছাড়া কাজ করা<br><b>English:</b> To improvise, to make decisions without planning or preparation<br><b>Example:</b> Without a script, the comedian flew by the seat of his pants.	
Fly High	<b>Bengali:</b> অস্থায়ীভাবে খুব সফল হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Be very successful, especially temporarily<br><b>Example:</b> The startup was flying high before the market crash.	
Fly Off The Handle	<b>Bengali:</b> হঠাৎ রেগে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Lose one's temper suddenly and unexpectedly<br><b>Example:</b> He flew off the handle when he saw the damage to his car.	
Follow In Someone's Footsteps	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো পদাঙ্ক অনুসরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> Follow the example laid down by someone else<br><b>Example:</b> She followed in her mother's footsteps and became a doctor.	
Follow Your Heart	<b>Bengali:</b> হৃদয়ের কথা শোনা<br><b>English:</b> Rely on one's deeper feelings and instincts when making a decision<br><b>Example:</b> When choosing a career, sometimes you just have to follow your heart.	
Food for Thought	<b>Bengali:</b> চিন্তার খোরাক<br><b>English:</b> Something that makes you think carefully<br><b>Example:</b> His speech about climate change was real food for thought.	
For a Song	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব কম দামে<br><b>English:</b> At very low cost<br><b>Example:</b> I bought this antique chair for a song at the garage sale.	
For Crying Out Loud	<b>Bengali:</b> চরম বিরক্তির অভিব্যক্তি<br><b>English:</b> An expression of extreme annoyance<br><b>Example:</b> For crying out loud, how many times do I have to explain this?	
Foul Play	<b>Bengali:</b> অপরাধ, বিশেষত হত্যা<br><b>English:</b> Crime, typically murder<br><b>Example:</b> The police suspect foul play in the businessman's sudden death.	
Fourth Estate	<b>Bengali:</b> সংবাদমাধ্যম<br><b>English:</b> The media and newspapers<br><b>Example:</b> The fourth estate plays a crucial role in democracy by holding politicians accountable.	
Fox in the Henhouse	<b>Bengali:</b> ঝামেলা সৃষ্টিকারী<br><b>English:</b> Someone who causes trouble<br><b>Example:</b> Hiring that gossip columnist was like putting a fox in the henhouse.	
Freak Out	<b>Bengali:</b> অস্বাভাবিক আচরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> A wildly irrational reaction or spell of behavior<br><b>Example:</b> Don't freak out when you see the mess in the kitchen.	
French Leave	<b>Bengali:</b> অনুমতি ছাড়া চলে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Absence without permission<br><b>Example:</b> The soldier took French leave and went to visit his girlfriend.	
Freudian Slip	<b>Bengali:</b> ভুলবশত সত্য কথা বলা<br><b>English:</b> Accidental use of an incorrect word; a revealing slip of the tongue<br><b>Example:</b> Calling his wife by his ex's name was an embarrassing Freudian slip.	
From Pillar to Post	<b>Bengali:</b> এদিক ওদিক ঘোরা<br><b>English:</b> From one place to another, in a forced, random way<br><b>Example:</b> He's been going from pillar to post trying to find a job.	
From Scratch	<b>Bengali:</b> একেবারে শুরু থেকে<br><b>English:</b> From individual ingredients, not using a prepared mix<br><b>Example:</b> She baked the cake from scratch using her grandmother's recipe.	
From Soup to Nuts	<b>Bengali:</b> সবকিছু; শুরু থেকে শেষ<br><b>English:</b> Everything; from beginning to end<br><b>Example:</b> The wedding planner handled everything from soup to nuts.	
From the Bottom of One's Heart	<b>Bengali:</b> হৃদয়ের গভীর থেকে<br><b>English:</b> Sincerely and with deep feeling<br><b>Example:</b> I thank you from the bottom of my heart for your kindness.	
FUBAR	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্পূর্ণ নষ্ট<br><b>English:</b> Hopelessly ruined, not working, messed up<br><b>Example:</b> The computer system is completely FUBAR after the virus attack.	
Full of the Joys of Spring	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত খুশি ও উৎসাহী<br><b>English:</b> Very happy, enthusiastic, and full of energy<br><b>Example:</b> She was full of the joys of spring after getting the promotion.Front	
Hobson's Choice	<b>Bengali:</b> খারাপ বিকল্পগুলির মধ্যে পছন্দ<br><b>English:</b> A choice among bad options<br><b>Example:</b> Accepting the pay cut or losing the job entirely was a Hobson's choice.	
Hold One's Liquor	<b>Bengali:</b> বেশি মদ খেয়েও প্রভাবিত না হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Be able to drink a large amount without being affected<br><b>Example:</b> He can hold his liquor better than anyone I know.	
Hold One's Peace	<b>Bengali:</b> চুপ থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Be silent<br><b>Example:</b> I wanted to argue, but decided to hold my peace.	
Hold the Phone	<b>Bengali:</b> একটু অপেক্ষা কর<br><b>English:</b> Wait a moment (whether you're on the phone or not)<br><b>Example:</b> Hold the phone - did you just say you won the lottery?	
Hold Your Horses	<b>Bengali:</b> থাম, এত উত্তেজিত হয়ো না<br><b>English:</b> Stop; restrain yourself; don't be so excited<br><b>Example:</b> Hold your horses! Let me explain before you get angry.	
Home Away from Home	<b>Bengali:</b> ঘরের মতো জায়গা<br><b>English:</b> A habitual hangout; a place one frequents often and where one feels welcome<br><b>Example:</b> The local coffee shop has become my home away from home.	
Home Truths	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন সত্য<br><b>English:</b> Honest, often painful criticism<br><b>Example:</b> It's time someone told him some home truths about his behavior.	
Honor System	<b>Bengali:</b> সততার উপর নির্ভর করে চলা<br><b>English:</b> A system of payments that relies on the honesty of those paying<br><b>Example:</b> The farm stand operates on the honor system - just leave money in the box.	
Hot Mess	<b>Bengali:</b> চরম বিশৃঙ্খল অবস্থা<br><b>English:</b> Something or someone in a state of extreme disorder<br><b>Example:</b> After the party, the house was a hot mess.	
Hot on the Heels (of)	<b>Bengali:</b> পিছু নেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> In close pursuit<br><b>Example:</b> The police were hot on the heels of the fleeing suspect.	
Hot Potato	<b>Bengali:</b> বিতর্কিত বিষয়<br><b>English:</b> A controversial subject or difficult project that is best avoided<br><b>Example:</b> Climate change is a political hot potato that many politicians avoid.	
I Wouldn't Put It Past (Someone)	<b>Bengali:</b> এই ব্যক্তির এটা করা সম্ভব<br><b>English:</b> I think it's quite possible that [this person] would do this<br><b>Example:</b> He's so competitive, I wouldn't put it past him to cheat.	
If It Had Been a Snake, It Would Have Bitten Me	<b>Bengali:</b> খুবই স্পষ্ট ছিল কিন্তু আমি দেখিনি<br><b>English:</b> It was very obvious, but I missed it<br><b>Example:</b> I spent an hour looking for my glasses - if it had been a snake, it would have bitten me!	
If the Shoe Fits, Wear It	<b>Bengali:</b> যদি এটা তোমার জন্য সত্যি হয় তাহলে মেনে নাও<br><b>English:</b> If this description of you is accurate, accept it<br><b>Example:</b> People say you're lazy - if the shoe fits, wear it.	
I'm All Ears	<b>Bengali:</b> আমি শুনছি, বলো<br><b>English:</b> You have my attention, so you should talk<br><b>Example:</b> You said you have exciting news - I'm all ears.	
In a Fog	<b>Bengali:</b> বিভ্রান্ত, অস্পষ্ট<br><b>English:</b> Confused, not mentally alert<br><b>Example:</b> After working all night, I'm in a fog this morning.	
In a Heartbeat	<b>Bengali:</b> তৎক্ষণাৎ<br><b>English:</b> Immediately. This is especially used in hypothetical situations<br><b>Example:</b> If they offered me that job, I'd take it in a heartbeat.	
In a Jam	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যায় পড়া<br><b>English:</b> In need of help, in a difficult spot<br><b>Example:</b> I'm in a jam - my car won't start and I'm late for work.	
In a New York Minute	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব দ্রুত<br><b>English:</b> Very quickly<br><b>Example:</b> He'd sell his soul for money in a New York minute.	
In a Nutshell	<b>Bengali:</b> সংক্ষেপে<br><b>English:</b> Expressed in a few words<br><b>Example:</b> In a nutshell, the project was a complete failure.	
In a Pickle	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যায় পড়া<br><b>English:</b> In need of help, in a difficult spot<br><b>Example:</b> I'm in a pickle - I promised to be at two places at the same time.	
In a Rut	<b>Bengali:</b> একঘেয়েমিতে আটকা<br><b>English:</b> Confined by routine, bored and seeking new experiences<br><b>Example:</b> I'm in a rut at work - doing the same thing every day.	
In Broad Daylight	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রকাশ্য দিবালোকে<br><b>English:</b> When something occurs in broad daylight, it means the event is clearly visible<br><b>Example:</b> The robbery happened in broad daylight on a busy street.	
In Clover	<b>Bengali:</b> আর্থিক সচ্ছলতা<br><b>English:</b> Benefiting from a positive financial situation<br><b>Example:</b> After winning the lottery, they're living in clover.	
In For a Penny, In for a Pound	<b>Bengali:</b> একবার শুরু করলে শেষ পর্যন্ত<br><b>English:</b> Committed to something even though the risks are increasing<br><b>Example:</b> We've already invested so much, in for a penny, in for a pound.	
In Full Swing	<b>Bengali:</b> পূর্ণ গতিতে<br><b>English:</b> When something, such as an event, gets into full swing, it is at its busiest or liveliest time<br><b>Example:</b> By midnight, the party was in full swing.	
In His Cups	<b>Bengali:</b> মাতাল<br><b>English:</b> Drunk<br><b>Example:</b> He tends to get emotional when he's in his cups.	
In Hot Water	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যায়<br><b>English:</b> In need of help; in trouble<br><b>Example:</b> I'll be in hot water if I'm late for this meeting.	
In One Fell Swoop	<b>Bengali:</b> এক ধাক্কায়<br><b>English:</b> All at once, in a single action<br><b>Example:</b> The company fired 200 employees in one fell swoop.	
In One's Element	<b>Bengali:</b> উপযুক্ত পরিবেশে<br><b>English:</b> In a situation which is entirely suitable, familiar, or enjoyable<br><b>Example:</b> She's in her element when teaching children.	
In Someone's Wheelhouse	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো দক্ষতার ক্ষেত্রে<br><b>English:</b> In someone's strongest area of competence or enthusiasm<br><b>Example:</b> Computer programming is right in his wheelhouse.	
In Touch	<b>Bengali:</b> যোগাযোগে<br><b>English:</b> In contact<br><b>Example:</b> We've stayed in touch since college.	
In the Blink of an Eye	<b>Bengali:</b> চোখের পলকে<br><b>English:</b> Quickly, seemingly instantaneously<br><b>Example:</b> In the blink of an eye, the magician made the rabbit disappear.	
In the Cards	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্ভাব্য<br><b>English:</b> Likely; likely to occur<br><b>Example:</b> A promotion might be in the cards for you this year.	
In the Crosshairs	<b>Bengali:</b> সমালোচনার লক্ষ্য<br><b>English:</b> Targeted for blame or criticism<br><b>Example:</b> After the scandal, the CEO was in the crosshairs.	
In the Dark	<b>Bengali:</b> অজ্ঞাত<br><b>English:</b> Not informed<br><b>Example:</b> The employees were kept in the dark about the merger.	
In the Driver's Seat	<b>Bengali:</b> নিয়ন্ত্রণে<br><b>English:</b> In a dominant position, in control<br><b>Example:</b> With the best product, we're in the driver's seat for negotiations.	
In the Hot Seat	<b>Bengali:</b> সমালোচনার মুখে<br><b>English:</b> Undergoing criticism or scrutiny; under pressure publicly<br><b>Example:</b> The politician was in the hot seat during the press conference.	
In the Interim	<b>Bengali:</b> মধ্যবর্তী সময়ে<br><b>English:</b> It denotes a period of time between something that ended and something that happened afterwards<br><b>Example:</b> The new manager starts next month; in the interim, I'll handle the team.	
In the Limelight, In the Spotlight	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রচারের আলোয়<br><b>English:</b> Receiving large amounts of publicity or attention<br><b>Example:</b> The young actor enjoys being in the limelight.	
In the Long Run	<b>Bengali:</b> দীর্ঘমেয়াদে<br><b>English:</b> Over an extended period of time<br><b>Example:</b> In the long run, this investment will pay off.	
In the Nick of Time	<b>Bengali:</b> ঠিক সময়ে<br><b>English:</b> Just in time; with no time to spare<br><b>Example:</b> The ambulance arrived in the nick of time.	
In the Pipeline	<b>Bengali:</b> কাজ চলছে<br><b>English:</b> Being prepared for the marketplace, being worked on<br><b>Example:</b> We have several new products in the pipeline.	
In the Red	<b>Bengali:</b> লোকসানে<br><b>English:</b> Losing money; (of a market index) below a specified starting point<br><b>Example:</b> The company has been in the red for three consecutive quarters.	
In the Same Boat	<b>Bengali:</b> একই অবস্থায়<br><b>English:</b> In a similar situation; similarly vulnerable<br><b>Example:</b> We're all in the same boat when it comes to job security.	
In the Toilet	<b>Bengali:</b> খারাপ অবস্থায়<br><b>English:</b> In disastrous condition<br><b>Example:</b> After the scandal, his reputation is in the toilet.	
In the Works	<b>Bengali:</b> কাজ চলছে<br><b>English:</b> Under development; coming soon<br><b>Example:</b> A sequel to the movie is in the works.	
Iron Out (Problems, Difficulties)	<b>Bengali:</b> সমাধান করা<br><b>English:</b> To resolve<br><b>Example:</b> We need to iron out these contract details before signing.	
Is the Pope Catholic?	<b>Bengali:</b> উত্তর কি স্পষ্ট নয়?<br><b>English:</b> Isn't the answer obvious?<br><b>Example:</b> Will I accept that job offer? Is the Pope Catholic?	
It Never Rains but It Pours	<b>Bengali:</b> দুর্ভাগ্য একসাথে আসে<br><b>English:</b> Bad luck and bad things tend to happen at the same time<br><b>Example:</b> First my car broke down, then I got sick - it never rains but it pours.	
It Takes Two to Tango	<b>Bengali:</b> দুজনে মিলেই ঝগড়া<br><b>English:</b> When something goes wrong involving two people, it's likely that they share the blame; cooperation is necessary<br><b>Example:</b> Don't blame just her for the argument - it takes two to tango.	
It Won't Fly	<b>Bengali:</b> এটা কাজ করবে না<br><b>English:</b> It won't work; it won't be approved<br><b>Example:</b> Your excuse for being late won't fly with the boss.	
Itchy Feet	<b>Bengali:</b> ভ্রমণপিপাসু<br><b>English:</b> A person who has itchy feet is someone who finds it difficult to stay in one place and likes to travel and discover new places<br><b>Example:</b> Spring always gives me itchy feet - I want to travel somewhere new.	
It's a Wash	<b>Bengali:</b> সমান সমান<br><b>English:</b> A positive and a negative development cancel each other out, so the situation has neither improved nor gotten worse<br><b>Example:</b> I saved money on gas but spent it on parking - it's a wash.	
It's All Greek to Me	<b>Bengali:</b> একেবারে বোঝা যায় না<br><b>English:</b> It is unintelligible, impossible to understand<br><b>Example:</b> This physics equation is all Greek to me.	
It's No Skin off My (Your) Nose	<b>Bengali:</b> আমার কোন ক্ষতি নেই<br><b>English:</b> The outcome will not affect me personally<br><b>Example:</b> If you want to quit, it's no skin off my nose.	
It's Not Over Till the Fat Lady Sings	<b>Bengali:</b> শেষ না হওয়া পর্যন্ত হাল ছেড়ো না<br><b>English:</b> Do not give up too soon; things may improve<br><b>Example:</b> We're behind in the game, but it's not over till the fat lady sings.	
It's Not Rocket Science	<b>Bengali:</b> এটা কঠিন নয়<br><b>English:</b> It's not difficult to understand<br><b>Example:</b> Changing a tire isn't rocket science - anyone can learn.	
I've Had It Up to Here	<b>Bengali:</b> আমার ধৈর্য শেষ<br><b>English:</b> My patience is almost exhausted<br><b>Example:</b> I've had it up to here with your constant complaining.	
Jam Session	<b>Bengali:</b> অনানুষ্ঠানিক সঙ্গীত পরিবেশনা<br><b>English:</b> Playing improvised music in an informal setting<br><b>Example:</b> The musicians had a jam session after the concert.	
Jim Crow	<b>Bengali:</b> জাতিগত বৈষম্য ব্যবস্থা<br><b>English:</b> The system of racial segregation in the American South prior to the American civil rights movement<br><b>Example:</b> The Jim Crow laws enforced racial segregation for decades.	
Join the Club	<b>Bengali:</b> আমিও একই অভিজ্ঞতা পেয়েছি<br><b>English:</b> I feel sympathy for you because I have experienced something similar<br><b>Example:</b> You failed the driving test? Join the club - so did I.	
Jump in with Both Feet	<b>Bengali:</b> পুরোপুরি মনোযোগ দিয়ে শুরু করা<br><b>English:</b> Begin a new experience wholeheartedly<br><b>Example:</b> When she started the new job, she jumped in with both feet.	
Jump on the Bandwagon	<b>Bengali:</b> ধারা অনুসরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> To follow a trend or craze<br><b>Example:</b> Everyone's jumping on the cryptocurrency bandwagon.	
Jump the Gun	<b>Bengali:</b> তাড়াহুড়ো করা<br><b>English:</b> Start doing something too soon<br><b>Example:</b> Don't jump the gun - wait for the official announcement.	
Jump the Shark	<b>Bengali:</b> সর্বোচ্চ মান পার করে খারাপ হতে থাকা<br><b>English:</b> To pass peak quality and begin to decline. Often used to describe television programs or movie series<br><b>Example:</b> The TV show jumped the shark in its fifth season.	
Jump the Track	<b>Bengali:</b> হঠাৎ বিষয় পরিবর্তন<br><b>English:</b> To shift suddenly from one activity or line of thought to another<br><b>Example:</b> The conversation jumped the track when someone mentioned politics.	
Jump Through Hoops	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন কাজ করে কাউকে সন্তুষ্ট করা<br><b>English:</b> Complete a series of tasks in order to satisfy someone<br><b>Example:</b> I had to jump through hoops to get approval for this project.	
Just Around the Corner	<b>Bengali:</b> শীঘ্রই ঘটবে<br><b>English:</b> Occurring soon<br><b>Example:</b> Spring is just around the corner.	
Just for the Record	<b>Bengali:</b> স্পষ্ট করে বলতে চাই<br><b>English:</b> I would like to make it clear that …<br><b>Example:</b> Just for the record, I never agreed to that proposal.	
Just What the Doctor Ordered	<b>Bengali:</b> ঠিক যা দরকার ছিল<br><b>English:</b> Exactly the thing that is or was needed to help improve something or make one feel better<br><b>Example:</b> A week at the beach was just what the doctor ordered.	
Keep (Something) at Bay	<b>Bengali:</b> দূরে রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Maintain a distance from something or someone<br><b>Example:</b> Regular exercise helps keep illness at bay.	
Keep a Stiff Upper Lip	<b>Bengali:</b> আবেগ নিয়ন্ত্রণ করা<br><b>English:</b> Control one's emotions; not give in to fear or grief<br><b>Example:</b> Despite the tragedy, she kept a stiff upper lip.	
Keep an Eye On	<b>Bengali:</b> নজর রাখা<br><b>English:</b> To keep an eye on something or someone is to watch it periodically, to keep it under surveillance<br><b>Example:</b> Can you keep an eye on my luggage while I'm gone?	
Keep an Eye Peeled	<b>Bengali:</b> সতর্ক থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Be observant; watch out for something<br><b>Example:</b> Keep an eye peeled for the exit sign.	
Keep It Under Your Hat	<b>Bengali:</b> গোপন রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Don't tell anyone; don't reveal this secret<br><b>Example:</b> I'm getting promoted, but keep it under your hat until it's official.	
Keep Someone at Arm's Length	<b>Bengali:</b> দূরত্ব বজায় রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Avoid close interaction or cooperation<br><b>Example:</b> I keep that gossipy coworker at arm's length.	
Keep Your Nose Clean	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যা এড়িয়ে চলা<br><b>English:</b> Avoid trouble or situations that compromise one's honesty<br><b>Example:</b> If you want to keep this job, keep your nose clean.	
Keep Your Powder Dry	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রস্তুত না হওয়া পর্যন্ত অপেক্ষা<br><b>English:</b> Do not attack until you are ready<br><b>Example:</b> Don't confront him yet - keep your powder dry until you have all the facts.	
Keeping One's Nose to the Grindstone	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠোর পরিশ্রম করা<br><b>English:</b> Working hard on something repetitive or tedious<br><b>Example:</b> He's been keeping his nose to the grindstone, preparing for the bar exam.	
Kick Ass, Kick Butt	<b>Bengali:</b> খারাপভাবে পরাজিত করা বা অসাধারণ হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> 1) Defeat badly; 2) be excellent or highly effective<br><b>Example:</b> Our team is going to kick ass in the championship.	
Kick the Bucket	<b>Bengali:</b> মারা যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To die<br><b>Example:</b> My old car finally kicked the bucket after 200,000 miles.	
Kick the Can Down the Road	<b>Bengali:</b> গুরুত্বপূর্ণ সিদ্ধান্ত স্থগিত রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Postpone an important decision<br><b>Example:</b> Instead of solving the budget crisis, Congress kicked the can down the road.	
Kill a Fly With an Elephant Gun	<b>Bengali:</b> ছোট সমস্যার জন্য বড় ব্যবস্থা<br><b>English:</b> Approach a problem with excessive measures<br><b>Example:</b> Hiring a lawyer for a parking ticket is like killing a fly with an elephant gun.	
Kill the Goose That Laid the Golden Egg	<b>Bengali:</b> লাভের উৎস ধ্বংস করা<br><b>English:</b> To destroy a source of ongoing profits or benefits<br><b>Example:</b> Firing their best salesperson would be killing the goose that laid the golden egg.	
Kill Two Birds with One Stone	<b>Bengali:</b> এক ঢিলে দুই পাখি মারা<br><b>English:</b> Act in such a way as to produce two desirable effects<br><b>Example:</b> By biking to work, I kill two birds with one stone - exercise and transportation.	
King of the Hill	<b>Bengali:</b> ক্ষেত্রের সেরা<br><b>English:</b> At the top of one's field; the most influential person in a given field or area<br><b>Example:</b> Microsoft was king of the hill in the software industry for decades.	
Kink in One's Neck	<b>Bengali:</b> ঘাড়ে ব্যথা<br><b>English:</b> A cramp in one's neck that causes pain<br><b>Example:</b> I woke up with a kink in my neck from sleeping wrong.	
Kiss and Make Up	<b>Bengali:</b> ঝগড়ার পর মিটমাট<br><b>English:</b> Make peace after an argument<br><b>Example:</b> The siblings always fight but then kiss and make up.	
Kith and Kin	<b>Bengali:</b> আত্মীয়স্বজন<br><b>English:</b> Family (collectively)<br><b>Example:</b> He invited all his kith and kin to the wedding.	
Knock on Wood; Touch Wood	<b>Bengali:</b> ভাগ্য ভাল থাকুক<br><b>English:</b> Let's hope I have good luck or continue to have good luck<br><b>Example:</b> I haven't been sick all year, knock on wood.	
Knock Some Sense Into	<b>Bengali:</b> কাউকে শিক্ষা দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To beat someone in order to teach him/her a lesson. May be used figuratively<br><b>Example:</b> Maybe losing his job will knock some sense into him.	
Knock Someone's Socks Off	<b>Bengali:</b> অবাক করে দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Amaze someone<br><b>Example:</b> Her performance will knock your socks off.	
Knock Up	<b>Bengali:</b> গর্ভবতী করা<br><b>English:</b> To impregnate a woman. Often used in the form knocked up<br><b>Example:</b> She got knocked up during her senior year of college.	
Knockout	<b>Bengali:</b> অসাধারণ সুন্দরী<br><b>English:</b> An extremely beautiful woman<br><b>Example:</b> In that dress, she's a real knockout.	
Know (Something) Like the Back of One's Hand	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব ভালভাবে জানা<br><b>English:</b> To be very familiar with something, especially an area<br><b>Example:</b> I know this neighborhood like the back of my hand.	
Larger Than Life	<b>Bengali:</b> মহৎ বা প্রভাবশালী হওয়ার অনুভূতি প্রকাশ করা<br><b>English:</b> Conveying a sense of greatness, imposing<br><b>Example:</b> The rock star had a larger than life personality.	
Last But Not Least	<b>Bengali:</b> আমি যা বলেছি তা গুরুত্বের ক্রমানুসারে নয়<br><b>English:</b> What I have just said does not reflect a ranking in importance<br><b>Example:</b> Last but not least, I'd like to thank my parents.	
Laughter is the Best Medicine	<b>Bengali:</b> অনেক হাসা শারীরিক বা মানসিক আঘাত থেকে পুনরুদ্ধারের একটি খুব কার্যকর উপায়<br><b>English:</b> Laughing a lot is a very effective means of recovering from physical or mental injury<br><b>Example:</b> After her divorce, she found that laughter is the best medicine.	
Learn the Ropes	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি কাজ বা ক্ষেত্রের সাথে আরো পরিচিত হওয়া; প্রশিক্ষিত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Become more familiar with a job or field of endeavor; be trained<br><b>Example:</b> It took me three months to learn the ropes at my new job.	
Leave Someone in the Lurch	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন পরিস্থিতিতে কাউকে ফেলে রেখে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Abandon someone in a difficult situation<br><b>Example:</b> When he quit suddenly, he left us in the lurch with no replacement.	
Lend an Ear	<b>Bengali:</b> শোনা<br><b>English:</b> Listen<br><b>Example:</b> She always lends an ear when I need to talk.	
Let Bygones Be Bygones	<b>Bengali:</b> অতীতের দ্বন্দ্ব ভুলে যেতে সম্মত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Agree to forget about a past conflict<br><b>Example:</b> Let's let bygones be bygones and start fresh.	
Let Off Steam	<b>Bengali:</b> রাগ ও হতাশা এমনভাবে প্রকাশ করা যাতে কোনো ক্ষতি না হয়<br><b>English:</b> To express anger and frustration in a way that does no damage<br><b>Example:</b> I need to go for a run to let off steam.	
Let One's Hair Down	<b>Bengali:</b> শিথিল হয়ে উপভোগ করা<br><b>English:</b> To relax and enjoy themselves<br><b>Example:</b> After the exam, the students let their hair down at the party.	
Let Sleeping Dogs Lie	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যায় নাড়াচাড়া এড়ানো; বিষয়গুলো একা ছেড়ে দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To avoid stirring up a problem; to leave things alone<br><b>Example:</b> I know you're curious about their divorce, but let sleeping dogs lie.	duplicate
Let the Cat Out of the Bag	<b>Bengali:</b> একটি গোপনীয়তা প্রকাশ করা, সাধারণত এমন গোপনীয়তা যা আপনি বা অন্যরা লুকিয়ে রাখার চেষ্টা করছেন<br><b>English:</b> Reveal a secret, usually a secret you or others are trying to keep<br><b>Example:</b> Don't let the cat out of the bag about the surprise party.	duplicate
Let the Genie Out of the Bottle	<b>Bengali:</b> এতদিন দমিয়ে রাখা কিছু প্রকাশ করা<br><b>English:</b> Reveal something hitherto suppressed<br><b>Example:</b> Once nuclear weapons were invented, we let the genie out of the bottle.	duplicate
Letter of the Law	<b>Bengali:</b> আইনের স্পষ্ট অর্থ, আইনের মূল উদ্দেশ্যের বিপরীতে<br><b>English:</b> The explicit meaning of a law, as opposed to the spirit of the law<br><b>Example:</b> He follows the letter of the law but ignores its spirit.	duplicate
Lick One's Wounds	<b>Bengali:</b> খারাপ পরাজয়ের পর বিশ্রাম নেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Rest after a bad defeat<br><b>Example:</b> After losing the election, he went home to lick his wounds.	duplicate
Life is A Bowl of Cherries	<b>Bengali:</b> জীবন চমৎকার বা খুবই আনন্দদায়ক<br><b>English:</b> Life is wonderful or very pleasant<br><b>Example:</b> When you're young and healthy, life is a bowl of cherries.	duplicate
Light a Fire Under Someone	<b>Bengali:</b> কাউকে কঠিন পরিশ্রম করতে অনুপ্রাণিত করা<br><b>English:</b> Inspire someone to work very hard<br><b>Example:</b> The coach lit a fire under the team during halftime.	duplicate
Light at the End of the Tunnel	<b>Bengali:</b> দীর্ঘ কষ্টের পর আশার আলো<br><b>English:</b> A sign of hope after a long period of difficulties<br><b>Example:</b> After months of unemployment, the job interview was light at the end of the tunnel.	duplicate
Like a Kid in a Candy Store	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিবেশ নিয়ে এতটাই উত্তেজিত হওয়া যে শিশুর মতো বা বোকার মতো আচরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> To be so excited about one's surroundings that one acts in a childlike or silly way<br><b>Example:</b> At the electronics store, he was like a kid in a candy store.	duplicate
Like a Moth to a Flame	<b>Bengali:</b> বিপদ সত্ত্বেও কিছু বা কারো প্রতি আকৃষ্ট হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Drawn to something or someone despite the dangers<br><b>Example:</b> He's drawn to risky investments like a moth to a flame.	duplicate
Like Father, Like Son	<b>Bengali:</b> ছেলেরা তাদের বাবার বৈশিষ্ট্য ও পছন্দ উত্তরাধিকার সূত্রে পায়, প্রায়ই না বুঝেই<br><b>English:</b> Sons inherit their fathers' traits and preferences, often even without realizing it<br><b>Example:</b> Both father and son are doctors - like father, like son.	duplicate
Like Shooting Fish in a Barrel	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত সহজ<br><b>English:</b> Very easy<br><b>Example:</b> Beating that weak team was like shooting fish in a barrel.	duplicate
Like Taking Candy from a Baby	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত সহজ<br><b>English:</b> Very easy<br><b>Example:</b> The exam was like taking candy from a baby.	duplicate
Like The Cat That Got The Cream	<b>Bengali:</b> বিশেষভাবে আত্মতুষ্ট দেখানো, প্রায়ই অন্যদের বিরক্তির কারণ<br><b>English:</b> Looking particularly self-satisfied, often to the annoyance of others<br><b>Example:</b> After getting the promotion, he looked like the cat that got the cream.	duplicate
Like Two Peas in a Pod	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রবল মিল থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Bearing a strong resemblance<br><b>Example:</b> The twins are like two peas in a pod - you can't tell them apart.	duplicate
Lion's Den	<b>Bengali:</b> যেকোনো বিপজ্জনক বা ভয়ানক জায়গা<br><b>English:</b> Any dangerous or frightening place<br><b>Example:</b> Walking into that hostile board meeting was like entering the lion's den.	duplicate
Lion's Share	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছুর সবচেয়ে বড় অংশ<br><b>English:</b> The largest part of something<br><b>Example:</b> The CEO gets the lion's share of the company's profits.	duplicate
Live Large	<b>Bengali:</b> বিলাসবহুল জীবনযাত্রা<br><b>English:</b> Have a luxurious lifestyle<br><b>Example:</b> After winning the lottery, they decided to live large.	duplicate
Living in Cloud Cuckooland	<b>Bengali:</b> অবাস্তব বা বোকামি বিশ্বাস বা পরিকল্পনা থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Having unrealistic or foolish beliefs or plans<br><b>Example:</b> If you think you'll get rich without working, you're living in cloud cuckooland.	duplicate
Living on Borrowed Time	<b>Bengali:</b> অসুস্থতা বা মৃত্যুর কাছাকাছি অভিজ্ঞতার পর, অনেকে বিশ্বাস করে তারা মৃত্যুকে ঠকিয়েছে<br><b>English:</b> Following an illness or near-death experience, many people believe they have cheated death<br><b>Example:</b> After the heart attack, he felt like he was living on borrowed time.	duplicate
Living Under a Rock	<b>Bengali:</b> গুরুত্বপূর্ণ ঘটনা সম্পর্কে অজ্ঞ। সাধারণত প্রশ্ন হিসেবে ব্যবহৃত<br><b>English:</b> Ignorant of important events. Usually used as a question: Have you been living under a rock?<br><b>Example:</b> You don't know about the election results? Have you been living under a rock?	duplicate
Loaded for Bear	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যার জন্য প্রস্তুত, চ্যালেঞ্জের জন্য ভালভাবে প্রস্তুত<br><b>English:</b> Prepared for problems, well prepared for a challenge<br><b>Example:</b> The lawyer came to court loaded for bear with evidence.	duplicate
Loan Shark	<b>Bengali:</b> একজন শোষণকারী ঋণদাতা; যে মরিয়া মানুষদের উচ্চ সুদে ঋণ দেয়<br><b>English:</b> A predatory lender; one who makes high-interest loans to desperate people<br><b>Example:</b> Avoid loan sharks - their interest rates are astronomical.	duplicate
Lock Horns	<b>Bengali:</b> তর্ক করা, দ্বন্দ্বে জড়ানো<br><b>English:</b> To lock horns is to argue, to come into conflict<br><b>Example:</b> The two CEOs locked horns over the merger terms.	duplicate
Long Shot	<b>Bengali:</b> সফলতার সম্ভাবনা কম এমন কিছু<br><b>English:</b> Something with little chance of success<br><b>Example:</b> Getting into Harvard is a long shot, but I'll apply anyway.	duplicate
Look the Other Way	<b>Bengali:</b> আইন বা নিয়ম ভঙ্গের বিষয়ে কোনো নোটিস না নেওয়া, অনানুষ্ঠানিকভাবে কিছু মেনে নেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Take no notice of violations of laws or rules, unofficially condone something<br><b>Example:</b> The security guard looked the other way when employees came in late.	duplicate
Look What the Cat Dragged In	<b>Bengali:</b> অবাঞ্ছিত কেউ এসেছে<br><b>English:</b> Someone unwelcome has arrived<br><b>Example:</b> Look what the cat dragged in - my annoying cousin just showed up.	duplicate
Loose Cannon	<b>Bengali:</b> নিয়ন্ত্রণের বাইরে কেউ; যে বেপরোয়াভাবে কথা বলে বা কাজ করে<br><b>English:</b> Someone out of control; someone who speaks or acts recklessly<br><b>Example:</b> That politician is a loose cannon who says whatever comes to mind.	duplicate
Lose It	<b>Bengali:</b> হঠাৎ করে যুক্তিসঙ্গতভাবে আচরণ বা চিন্তা করতে অক্ষম হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To suddenly become unable to behave or think in a sensible way<br><b>Example:</b> When I saw the mess, I completely lost it.	duplicate
Lose One's Touch	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু করার দক্ষতায় পতন ভোগ করা<br><b>English:</b> Suffer a decline in one's skill at doing something<br><b>Example:</b> The chef seems to have lost his touch - this meal is terrible.	duplicate
Lose the Thread	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো যুক্তি অনুসরণ করতে অক্ষম হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Be unable to follow someone's reasoning<br><b>Example:</b> I lost the thread of his argument when he started talking about philosophy.	duplicate
Love at First Sight	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রথম দেখাতেই কারো প্রেমে পড়া<br><b>English:</b> Falling in love with somebody the first time you see them<br><b>Example:</b> It was love at first sight when they met at the coffee shop.	duplicate
Love Rat	<b>Bengali:</b> যে তার সঙ্গীর সাথে প্রতারণা করে<br><b>English:</b> Somebody who cheats on his/her partner<br><b>Example:</b> She dumped him when she found out he was a love rat.	duplicate
Love Someone With All of One's Heart And Soul	<b>Bengali:</b> কাউকে সম্পূর্ণভাবে ভালোবাসা<br><b>English:</b> To love someone completely<br><b>Example:</b> Despite their problems, she loves him with all her heart and soul.	duplicate
Low-Hanging Fruit	<b>Bengali:</b> কাজের সহজ অংশ; সহজে পাওয়া যায় এমন সমাধান<br><b>English:</b> Easy parts of a task; solutions easy to obtain<br><b>Example:</b> Let's tackle the low-hanging fruit first before addressing complex issues.	duplicate
Lower the Boom	<b>Bengali:</b> শাস্তি কার্যকর করা; কঠোরভাবে তিরস্কার করা<br><b>English:</b> Implement a punishment; reprimand severely<br><b>Example:</b> The principal lowered the boom on students caught cheating.Front	duplicate
Game of Chicken	<b>Bengali:</b> সাহসিকতার পরীক্ষা<br><b>English:</b> A conflict situation in which neither side will back down for fear of seeming cowardly<br><b>Example:</b> The trade war became a game of chicken between the two superpowers.	
Get A Charley Horse	<b>Bengali:</b> হাত বা পায়ে খিঁচুনি হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To develop a cramp in the arm or the leg<br><b>Example:</b> I got a charley horse in my calf during the marathon.	
Get A Word In Edgewise	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো কথার ফাঁকে কিছু বলতে পারা<br><b>English:</b> Be able to say something while someone else is talking a lot<br><b>Example:</b> She talks so much, I can't get a word in edgewise.	
Get Along (with Someone)	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো সাথে ভাল সম্পর্ক রাখা<br><b>English:</b> To have a satisfactory relationship<br><b>Example:</b> I get along well with my new roommate.	
Get Bent Out of Shape	<b>Bengali:</b> রেগে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Become angry, upset<br><b>Example:</b> Don't get bent out of shape over a simple mistake.	
Get Carried Away	<b>Bengali:</b> অতিরিক্ত উৎসাহী হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Become overly enthusiastic<br><b>Example:</b> I got carried away shopping and spent my entire paycheck.	
Get In on the Ground Floor	<b>Bengali:</b> শুরুতেই যোগ দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Invest in or join something while it is still small<br><b>Example:</b> I wish I had gotten in on the ground floor with that tech startup.	
Get in Shape	<b>Bengali:</b> শারীরিক অবস্থা উন্নত করা<br><b>English:</b> Undertake a program of physical conditioning<br><b>Example:</b> I need to get in shape before the summer beach season.	
Get Off Scot Free	<b>Bengali:</b> দোষী হয়েও শাস্তি এড়ানো<br><b>English:</b> Be accused of wrongdoing but pay no penalty at all<br><b>Example:</b> Despite the evidence, the corrupt politician got off scot free.	
Get One's Ducks in a Row	<b>Bengali:</b> সবকিছু গুছিয়ে রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Have everything organized; get oneself organized<br><b>Example:</b> Before starting the business, I need to get my ducks in a row.	
Get One's Hands Dirty	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন কাজে হাত দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To do the unpleasant parts of a job<br><b>Example:</b> The CEO isn't afraid to get his hands dirty and work on the factory floor.	
Get Someone's Goat	<b>Bengali:</b> কাউকে গভীরভাবে বিরক্ত করা<br><b>English:</b> To irritate someone deeply<br><b>Example:</b> His constant whistling really gets my goat.	
Get To Grips With	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু বুঝতে ও মোকাবেলা করতে শুরু করা<br><b>English:</b> To begin to understand and deal with something<br><b>Example:</b> I'm still trying to get to grips with the new software.	
Get the Ball Rolling	<b>Bengali:</b> কোন প্রক্রিয়া শুরু করা<br><b>English:</b> Do something to begin a process<br><b>Example:</b> Let's get the ball rolling on this project by scheduling our first meeting.	
Get the Picture	<b>Bengali:</b> বিষয়টি বোঝা<br><b>English:</b> Understand what's happening<br><b>Example:</b> You don't want me here anymore - I get the picture.	
Get the Runaround	<b>Bengali:</b> অস্পষ্ট বা এড়িয়ে যাওয়া উত্তর পাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Be given an unclear or evasive answer to a question<br><b>Example:</b> I've been getting the runaround from customer service all week.	
Get the Sack, Be Sacked	<b>Bengali:</b> চাকরি হারানো<br><b>English:</b> To be fired<br><b>Example:</b> He got the sack for consistently arriving late to work.	
Get the Third Degree	<b>Bengali:</b> বিস্তারিত জিজ্ঞাসাবাদের মুখোমুখি হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To be questioned in great detail about something<br><b>Example:</b> When I came home late, my parents gave me the third degree.	
Get Wind of	<b>Bengali:</b> শুনতে পাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Hear about<br><b>Example:</b> If the boss gets wind of this mistake, we'll all be in trouble.	
Get With the Program	<b>Bengali:</b> অন্যরা যা জানে তা বোঝা<br><b>English:</b> Figure out what everyone else already knows<br><b>Example:</b> You need to get with the program - we're using the new system now.	
Give and Take	<b>Bengali:</b> আপস-মীমাংসা<br><b>English:</b> Negotiations, the process of compromise<br><b>Example:</b> Marriage requires a lot of give and take from both partners.	
Give 'em Hell	<b>Bengali:</b> জোরালোভাবে মতামত প্রকাশ করা<br><b>English:</b> Express something passionately to a group<br><b>Example:</b> The coach told the team to give 'em hell in the championship game.	
Give Lip Service to	<b>Bengali:</b> মুখে সমর্থন করা কিন্তু কাজ না করা<br><b>English:</b> Talk about supporting something without taking any concrete action<br><b>Example:</b> The company gives lip service to environmental protection but doesn't follow through.	
Give One's Two Cents	<b>Bengali:</b> মতামত দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Offer an opinion, suggest something<br><b>Example:</b> If I may give my two cents, I think we should postpone the meeting.	
Give Someone a Holler	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো সাথে যোগাযোগ করা<br><b>English:</b> Contact someone<br><b>Example:</b> Give me a holler when you're ready to leave.	
Give Someone a Piece of Your Mind	<b>Bengali:</b> রেগে গিয়ে মতামত জানানো<br><b>English:</b> Angrily tell someone what you think<br><b>Example:</b> I'm going to give that rude clerk a piece of my mind.	
Give Someone a Run for Their Money	<b>Bengali:</b> নেতার সাথে কার্যকরভাবে প্রতিযোগিতা করা<br><b>English:</b> Compete effectively with the leader in a particular field<br><b>Example:</b> The young tennis player gave the champion a run for his money.	
Give Someone an Earful	<b>Bengali:</b> রেগে গিয়ে কারো কাছে মতামত প্রকাশ করা<br><b>English:</b> Angrily express an opinion to someone<br><b>Example:</b> When he came home drunk, his wife gave him an earful.	
Give Someone the Cold Shoulder	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো প্রতি শীতল আচরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> Act hostile toward someone; to ignore, snub<br><b>Example:</b> Ever since the argument, she's been giving me the cold shoulder.	
Give Someone The Old Heave-Ho	<b>Bengali:</b> কাউকে বরখাস্ত করা<br><b>English:</b> Fire someone, remove someone from a group or team<br><b>Example:</b> After the scandal, the board gave the CEO the old heave-ho.	
Give Something a Whirl	<b>Bengali:</b> অপরিচিত কিছু চেষ্টা করা<br><b>English:</b> Attempt something without being totally familiar with it<br><b>Example:</b> I've never tried sushi, but I'll give it a whirl.	
Give the Green Light	<b>Bengali:</b> অনুমতি দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Approve something; allow something to proceed<br><b>Example:</b> The committee gave the green light for the new construction project.	
Go Along (With)	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছুতে সম্মত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Agree to something, often provisionally<br><b>Example:</b> I'll go along with your plan, but I have some reservations.	
Go Ape	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রবল উত্তেজনা বা রাগ প্রকাশ করা<br><b>English:</b> Express wild excitement or anger<br><b>Example:</b> The fans went ape when their team scored the winning goal.	
Go Ballistic	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রচণ্ড রেগে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Fly into a rage<br><b>Example:</b> My dad went ballistic when he saw the dent in his car.	
Go Bananas	<b>Bengali:</b> পাগল হয়ে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To become irrational or crazy<br><b>Example:</b> The crowd went bananas when the rock star appeared on stage.	
Go Belly Up	<b>Bengali:</b> দেউলিয়া হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To go bankrupt<br><b>Example:</b> The restaurant went belly up after only six months.	
Go Berserk	<b>Bengali:</b> উন্মাদ হয়ে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To go crazy<br><b>Example:</b> He went berserk when he found out someone had stolen his bike.	
Go Bonkers	<b>Bengali:</b> পাগল বা উন্মত্ত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To be or become wild, restless, irrational, or crazy<br><b>Example:</b> Staying indoors for weeks made him go bonkers.	
Go Cold Turkey	<b>Bengali:</b> হঠাৎ নেশা ছেড়ে দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Stop using an addictive substance suddenly, without tapering off<br><b>Example:</b> He quit smoking by going cold turkey - no patches or gum.	
Go Down in Flames	<b>Bengali:</b> চরমভাবে ব্যর্থ হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Fail in a spectacular way<br><b>Example:</b> His presentation went down in flames when the projector stopped working.	
Go Mental	<b>Bengali:</b> হঠাৎ প্রচণ্ড রেগে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To suddenly become extremely angry<br><b>Example:</b> She went mental when she saw her ruined garden.	
Go Nuclear	<b>Bengali:</b> চরম ব্যবস্থা নেওয়া; প্রচণ্ড রেগে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Use an extreme measure; become extremely angry<br><b>Example:</b> If they don't respond soon, we'll have to go nuclear with legal action.	
Go Nuts	<b>Bengali:</b> পাগল হয়ে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To become crazy<br><b>Example:</b> The kids went nuts when they saw all the presents under the tree.	
Go Off Half-Cocked	<b>Bengali:</b> অপরিপক্কভাবে কিছু করা<br><b>English:</b> To say or do something prematurely, with a negative effect<br><b>Example:</b> Don't go off half-cocked - think this through carefully first.	
Go Off the Deep End	<b>Bengali:</b> অপ্রত্যাশিতভাবে রেগে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To unexpectedly become very angry, especially without a good reason<br><b>Example:</b> He went off the deep end when I suggested changing the meeting time.	
Go Off The Rails	<b>Bengali:</b> ভুল পথে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To go wrong, to begin acting strangely or badly<br><b>Example:</b> The project went off the rails when the key team member quit.	
Go Out on a Limb	<b>Bengali:</b> ঝুঁকিপূর্ণ অবস্থানে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Assert something that may not be true; put oneself in a vulnerable position<br><b>Example:</b> I'll go out on a limb and say this will be our best year yet.	
Go Pear-Shaped	<b>Bengali:</b> ব্যর্থ হওয়া; ভুল হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To fail; to go wrong<br><b>Example:</b> The dinner party went pear-shaped when the oven broke down.	
Go See a Man About a Dog	<b>Bengali:</b> টয়লেটে যাওয়া (কৌশলে বলা)<br><b>English:</b> Go to the bathroom (euphemism)<br><b>Example:</b> Excuse me, I need to go see a man about a dog.	
Go to the Dogs	<b>Bengali:</b> নষ্ট হয়ে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To become disordered, to decay<br><b>Example:</b> This neighborhood has really gone to the dogs since the factory closed.	
Go to the Mattresses	<b>Bengali:</b> যুদ্ধে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To go into battle<br><b>Example:</b> When negotiations failed, both companies went to the mattresses in a price war.	
Go the Extra Mile	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রত্যাশার চেয়ে বেশি চেষ্টা করা<br><b>English:</b> Put forth greater-than-expected effort<br><b>Example:</b> She always goes the extra mile to help her customers.	
Go Under the Knife	<b>Bengali:</b> অপারেশন করানো<br><b>English:</b> Undergo surgery<br><b>Example:</b> He's going under the knife next week for his knee replacement.	
Go Viral	<b>Bengali:</b> ইন্টারনেটে দ্রুত ছড়িয়ে পড়া<br><b>English:</b> Begin to spread rapidly on the Internet<br><b>Example:</b> The cat video went viral and got millions of views overnight.	
Go with the Flow	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিস্থিতির সাথে মানিয়ে নেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To accept the way things naturally seem to be going<br><b>Example:</b> I don't have strong preferences for dinner - I'll just go with the flow.	
Grab (Take) the Bull by the Horns	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যার মোকাবেলায় দৃঢ়ভাবে এগিয়ে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To begin forthrightly to deal with a problem<br><b>Example:</b> Instead of worrying about debt, he grabbed the bull by the horns and got a second job.	
Grasp (Grab) at Straws	<b>Bengali:</b> হতাশার মধ্যে শেষ চেষ্টা করা<br><b>English:</b> To take desperate actions with little hope of success<br><b>Example:</b> Hiring that expensive consultant was grasping at straws.	
Grease Monkey	<b>Bengali:</b> যন্ত্রবিদ, বিশেষত গাড়ির মিস্ত্রি<br><b>English:</b> A mechanic, especially an auto mechanic<br><b>Example:</b> The grease monkey fixed my car's engine in no time.	
Grease the Wheels	<b>Bengali:</b> কাজ সহজ করার জন্য কিছু করা<br><b>English:</b> Do something to make an operation run smoothly<br><b>Example:</b> A small donation helped grease the wheels for the permit approval.	
Greasy Spoon	<b>Bengali:</b> সস্তা রেস্তোরাঁ<br><b>English:</b> An inexpensive restaurant that fries foods on a grill<br><b>Example:</b> We stopped at a greasy spoon for breakfast during our road trip.	
Green Around the Gills	<b>Bengali:</b> অসুস্থ দেখাচ্ছে<br><b>English:</b> To look sick<br><b>Example:</b> After the boat ride, he looked green around the gills.	
Green as Grass	<b>Bengali:</b> অনভিজ্ঞ; নতুন<br><b>English:</b> Lacking training, naive; often said of young people in new jobs<br><b>Example:</b> The new intern is green as grass but eager to learn.	
Grind One's Teeth	<b>Bengali:</b> চুপচাপ রাগ সহ্য করা<br><b>English:</b> Be very annoyed or angry about something without being able to say anything<br><b>Example:</b> I had to grind my teeth when the boss took credit for my work.	
Guilty Pleasure	<b>Bengali:</b> অপরাধবোধ নিয়ে কিছু উপভোগ করা<br><b>English:</b> Enjoying something which is not generally held in high regard while feeling guilty<br><b>Example:</b> Reality TV shows are my guilty pleasure.	
Guinea Pig	<b>Bengali:</b> পরীক্ষার বিষয়<br><b>English:</b> A test subject, a person who is used as a test<br><b>Example:</b> The new employees were guinea pigs for the experimental training program.	
Hail Mary	<b>Bengali:</b> শেষ চেষ্টা, হতাশাজনক প্রচেষ্টা<br><b>English:</b> A desperate, last-ditch attempt<br><b>Example:</b> With seconds left, the quarterback threw a Hail Mary pass.	
Hair of the Dog (That Bit You)	<b>Bengali:</b> মাতালতার পর একই মদ একটু খাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> A small amount of the alcoholic beverage that caused your hangover<br><b>Example:</b> He needed some hair of the dog to cure his hangover.	
Hands are Tied	<b>Bengali:</b> হাত বাঁধা, অসহায়<br><b>English:</b> You are prevented from doing something. It is not within your power<br><b>Example:</b> I'd love to give you a raise, but my hands are tied by company policy.	
Hands Down	<b>Bengali:</b> নিঃসন্দেহে, অবশ্যই<br><b>English:</b> Undoubtedly<br><b>Example:</b> She's hands down the best singer in the competition.	
Hang It Up	<b>Bengali:</b> অবসর নেওয়া, ছেড়ে দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To retire, to end an activity one has pursued for a long time<br><b>Example:</b> After 30 years of teaching, she decided to hang it up.	
Hang Tough	<b>Bengali:</b> দৃঢ় থাকা, অটল থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Maintain one's resolve<br><b>Example:</b> Hang tough - we'll get through this difficult period.	
Hanging by a Thread	<b>Bengali:</b> খুবই বিপদের মধ্যে<br><b>English:</b> In great danger of elimination or failure<br><b>Example:</b> His job is hanging by a thread after the latest mistake.	
Happy-Go-Lucky	<b>Bengali:</b> সর্বদা খুশি ও নির্ভাবনা<br><b>English:</b> If you are a happy-go-lucky person, you are cheerful and carefree all the time<br><b>Example:</b> Despite all her problems, she maintains a happy-go-lucky attitude.	
Hard Nut to Crack	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন সমস্যা বা কঠিন ব্যক্তি<br><b>English:</b> A difficult problem or a difficult person<br><b>Example:</b> Getting him to agree to the proposal will be a hard nut to crack.	
Has the Cat Got Your Tongue?	<b>Bengali:</b> কেন কিছু বলছ না?<br><b>English:</b> Why are you not saying anything?<br><b>Example:</b> You've been quiet all evening - has the cat got your tongue?	
Hat Trick	<b>Bengali:</b> পরপর তিনটি সাফল্য<br><b>English:</b> Scoring three goals in hockey or soccer, or accomplishing three of anything<br><b>Example:</b> The striker scored a hat trick in the championship game.	
Hatchet Job	<b>Bengali:</b> ইচ্ছাকৃত ক্ষতিকর সমালোচনা<br><b>English:</b> A strong attack on someone's reputation; intentionally destructive criticism<br><b>Example:</b> The newspaper did a hatchet job on the politician's character.	
Haul Over the Coals	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠোর তিরস্কার করা<br><b>English:</b> To scold someone severely<br><b>Example:</b> The boss hauled me over the coals for missing the deadline.	
Have (one's) head in the clouds	<b>Bengali:</b> বাস্তবতার সাথে সংযোগ হারানো<br><b>English:</b> Not know what is happening around you or out of touch with reality<br><b>Example:</b> He has his head in the clouds and doesn't realize how serious this is.	
Have A Ball	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব আনন্দ করা<br><b>English:</b> To have a very enjoyable time<br><b>Example:</b> The kids had a ball at the amusement park.	
Have a Bone to Pick (with Someone)	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো সাথে ঝগড়া বাধানো<br><b>English:</b> To want to discuss something someone has done that has angered or annoyed you<br><b>Example:</b> I have a bone to pick with you about those comments you made.	
Have a Chip on One's Shoulder	<b>Bengali:</b> রাগ পুষে রাখা<br><b>English:</b> To harbor resentment; to have an angry attitude<br><b>Example:</b> Ever since he was passed over for promotion, he's had a chip on his shoulder.	
Have a Dog in the Hunt	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতিযোগিতায় কাউকে সমর্থন করা<br><b>English:</b> To support a certain person in a competition<br><b>Example:</b> I don't have a dog in this hunt - I don't care who wins.	
Have a Lead Foot	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব জোরে গাড়ি চালানোর প্রবণতা<br><b>English:</b> A tendency to drive very fast<br><b>Example:</b> My brother has a lead foot - he's always getting speeding tickets.	
Have a Lot on One's Plate	<b>Bengali:</b> অনেক কাজে ব্যস্ত থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Be busy, be in the middle of many ongoing tasks<br><b>Example:</b> I can't take on another project - I already have a lot on my plate.	
Have a Lot Riding On (Something)	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছুর সফলতার উপর নির্ভর করা<br><b>English:</b> Be depending on the successful outcome or development of something<br><b>Example:</b> I have a lot riding on this job interview - I really need the work.	
Have a Nose for (Something)	<b>Bengali:</b> কোন কিছুতে প্রাকৃতিক দক্ষতা<br><b>English:</b> To have natural ability at something, a talent for finding something<br><b>Example:</b> She has a nose for finding good bargains at thrift stores.	
Have a Screw Loose	<b>Bengali:</b> একটু পাগলাটে<br><b>English:</b> Be slightly unbalanced or crazy<br><b>Example:</b> Anyone who would try that stunt must have a screw loose.	
Have a Tough Row to Hoe	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন পরিস্থিতিতে কাজ করা<br><b>English:</b> Be faced with a task that is difficult because of unfavorable conditions<br><b>Example:</b> Starting a business during a recession means you have a tough row to hoe.	
Have A Whale of A Time	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব মজা করা<br><b>English:</b> To enjoy yourself very much<br><b>Example:</b> We had a whale of a time at the beach vacation.	
Have an Ace Up One's Sleeve	<b>Bengali:</b> গোপন সুবিধা থাকা<br><b>English:</b> To have a hidden advantage<br><b>Example:</b> Don't worry about the negotiation - I have an ace up my sleeve.	
Have Bigger Fish to Fry	<b>Bengali:</b> আরও গুরুত্বপূর্ণ কাজ থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Have more important things to do<br><b>Example:</b> I can't worry about office gossip - I have bigger fish to fry.	
Have Egg on Your Face	<b>Bengali:</b> বিব্রত হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> They are made to look foolish or embarrassed<br><b>Example:</b> When his prediction proved wrong, he had egg on his face.	
Have Foot-in-Mouth Disease	<b>Bengali:</b> বোকা ভুলে নিজেকে বিব্রত করা<br><b>English:</b> To embarrass oneself through a silly mistake<br><b>Example:</b> I have foot-in-mouth disease - I always say the wrong thing.	
Have Hand of Aces/Hold All the Aces	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব শক্তিশালী অবস্থানে থাকা<br><b>English:</b> To be in a very strong position in a competition<br><b>Example:</b> In the merger talks, our company holds all the aces.	
Have It Out with Someone	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো সাথে ঝগড়া করে সমাধান করা<br><b>English:</b> To have an argument with someone in order to settle a dispute<br><b>Example:</b> I need to have it out with my roommate about the mess.	
Have One Foot in The Grave	<b>Bengali:</b> মৃত্যুর কাছাকাছি<br><b>English:</b> To be near death (usually because of old age or illness)<br><b>Example:</b> At 95, he jokes that he has one foot in the grave.	
Have One Over the Eight	<b>Bengali:</b> সামান্য মাতাল<br><b>English:</b> A person is slightly drunk<br><b>Example:</b> After the office party, he clearly had one over the eight.	
Have One Too Many	<b>Bengali:</b> বেশি মদ খাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Drink too much alcohol<br><b>Example:</b> I think I had one too many at the wedding reception.	
Have One's Cake and Eat It, Too	<b>Bengali:</b> দুই বিপরীত জিনিস চাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To want two incompatible things (usually used in the negative)<br><b>Example:</b> You can't have your cake and eat it too - either save money or spend it.	
Have Skin in the Game	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু ঝুঁকি নিয়ে কাজ করা<br><b>English:</b> Be risking something in an undertaking<br><b>Example:</b> I'll listen to your advice more seriously when you have skin in the game.	
Have the game in the Bag	<b>Bengali:</b> জয় নিশ্চিত<br><b>English:</b> Be certain to win<br><b>Example:</b> With a 20-point lead, they thought they had the game in the bag.	
Have the Hots for (Somebody)	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো প্রতি আকৃষ্ট হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To be (sexually) attracted to somebody<br><b>Example:</b> It's obvious he has the hots for his coworker.	
Have the Time of Your Life	<b>Bengali:</b> জীবনের সেরা সময় কাটানো<br><b>English:</b> To have a very fun, exciting, or enjoyable time<br><b>Example:</b> The kids had the time of their lives at Disney World.	
Have Your Nose in the Air	<b>Bengali:</b> অহংকারী মনোভাব<br><b>English:</b> Have a snobbish or disdainful attitude<br><b>Example:</b> Ever since she got rich, she has her nose in the air.	
Have Your Say	<b>Bengali:</b> মতামত প্রকাশ করা<br><b>English:</b> Express your opinion on something<br><b>Example:</b> Everyone will have their say at tomorrow's town hall meeting.	
Have Your Thumb Up Your Ass	<b>Bengali:</b> কোন কাজ না থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Have nothing to do<br><b>Example:</b> Instead of having your thumb up your ass, why don't you help us?	
He Who Laughs Last Laughs Best	<b>Bengali:</b> যে শেষে হাসে সে ভাল হাসে<br><b>English:</b> Being victorious is often a matter of simply surviving a conflict<br><b>Example:</b> They mocked his business idea, but he who laughs last laughs best.	
He Would Put Legs Under A Chicken	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব বেশি কথা বলা<br><b>English:</b> He will talk your head off; he is very talkative<br><b>Example:</b> Avoid sitting next to him at dinner - he would put legs under a chicken.

Head and Shoulders Above	<b>Bengali:</b> অনেক উন্নত<br><b>English:</b> Far superior to<br><b>Example:</b> Her performance is head and shoulders above the rest of the team.

Hell for Leather	<b>Bengali:</b> যত দ্রুত সম্ভব<br><b>English:</b> Very fast, as fast as possible<br><b>Example:</b> When he saw the police, he ran hell for leather.	
High as a Kite	<b>Bengali:</b> মাদকাসক্ত অবস্থা<br><b>English:</b> Strongly under the influence of drugs or intoxicants<br><b>Example:</b> After the surgery, the medication left him high as a kite.

Hit a Wall	<b>Bengali:</b> হঠাৎ অগ্রগতি থেমে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Suddenly stop making forward progress<br><b>Example:</b> After working for 12 hours, I hit a wall and couldn't concentrate anymore.

Tongue-in-Cheek	<b>Bengali:</b> ব্যঙ্গাত্মকভাবে বলা; গুরুত্ব সহকারে নেওয়ার জন্য নয়<br><b>English:</b> Said ironically; not meant to be taken seriously<br><b>Example:</b> His praise was clearly tongue-in-cheek.	
Too Busy Fighting Alligators to Drain the Swamp	<b>Bengali:</b> একাধিক সমস্যায় এত ব্যস্ত যে বড় চিত্র মনে রাখতে পারা যায় না<br><b>English:</b> So occupied with multiple challenges that one can't keep the big picture in mind<br><b>Example:</b> We're too busy fighting alligators to drain the swamp.

Touch One's Heart	<b>Bengali:</b> আবেগপ্রবণভাবে প্রভাবিত করা<br><b>English:</b> Affect someone emotionally, be touching<br><b>Example:</b> Her story about overcoming poverty really touched my heart.	
Touch Water	<b>Bengali:</b> জাহাজ চালু করা<br><b>English:</b> Be launched. Said of a boat<br><b>Example:</b> The new yacht will touch water next month.	
Tough Cookie	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব দৃঢ়প্রতিজ্ঞ ব্যক্তি<br><b>English:</b> A very determined person<br><b>Example:</b> Don't underestimate her - she's a tough cookie.	
Tough Sledding	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন অগ্রগতি<br><b>English:</b> Difficult progress<br><b>Example:</b> Getting the project approved has been tough sledding.	
Train Wreck	<b>Bengali:</b> যা বিপর্যয়করভাবে ঘটে<br><b>English:</b> Anything that develops in a disastrous way<br><b>Example:</b> The product launch was a complete train wreck.	
Trash Talk	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতিপক্ষের প্রতি অপমানজনক কথা<br><b>English:</b> Insults directed at one's opponent in a sporting event or contest<br><b>Example:</b> The players engaged in trash talk before the big game.	
Tread Water	<b>Bengali:</b> বর্তমান অবস্থা বজায় রাখা<br><b>English:</b> Maintain a current situation without improvement or decline<br><b>Example:</b> The company is just treading water until the economy improves.	
Trial Balloon	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো বা জনগণের প্রতিক্রিয়া পরীক্ষা<br><b>English:</b> A test of someone's or the public's reaction<br><b>Example:</b> The politician floated a trial balloon about raising taxes.	
Trip the Light Fantastic	<b>Bengali:</b> ভালো নাচা<br><b>English:</b> Dance well; do ballroom dancing<br><b>Example:</b> They tripped the light fantastic at the wedding reception.	
Turn a Blind Eye	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু না দেখার ভান করা<br><b>English:</b> Choose not to notice something<br><b>Example:</b> The manager turned a blind eye to employees leaving early on Friday.	
Turn on a Dime	<b>Bengali:</b> দ্রুত দিক বা অবস্থান পরিবর্তন করা<br><b>English:</b> Quickly reverse direction or position<br><b>Example:</b> Market conditions can turn on a dime in this business.	
Turn Someone Inside Out	<b>Bengali:</b> তীব্র আবেগিক অশান্তি সৃষ্টি করা<br><b>English:</b> To cause strong emotional turmoil; to completely change someone<br><b>Example:</b> The betrayal turned him inside out with grief.	
Turn Something on Its Head	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু উল্টে দেওয়া, নতুন উপায়ে করা<br><b>English:</b> Reverse something, cause something to be done in a new way<br><b>Example:</b> The internet turned traditional retail on its head.	
Turn Turtle	<b>Bengali:</b> উল্টে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Capsize, turn over<br><b>Example:</b> The boat turned turtle in the rough seas.	
Turn the Corner	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যার পর উন্নতি শুরু করা<br><b>English:</b> To begin to improve after a problem<br><b>Example:</b> The patient has turned the corner and is recovering well.	
Turn the Tables	<b>Bengali:</b> পরিস্থিতি উল্টে দেওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Reverse a situation<br><b>Example:</b> She turned the tables on her critics with a brilliant speech.	
Turnabout Is Fair Play	<b>Bengali:</b> অন্যের উপর যে কষ্ট দিয়েছো, তাই ভোগ করা ন্যায্য<br><b>English:</b> If you suffer from the same suffering you have inflicted on others, that's only fair<br><b>Example:</b> He complained when I was late, but turnabout is fair play.	
Twenty-Four Seven	<b>Bengali:</b> যেকোনো সময়<br><b>English:</b> At any time<br><b>Example:</b> The convenience store is open twenty-four seven.	
Twist the Knife (in Deeper)	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো কষ্ট আরো বাড়ানো<br><b>English:</b> Make someone's suffering worse<br><b>Example:</b> Mentioning her ex-boyfriend was twisting the knife deeper.	
Two a Penny	<b>Bengali:</b> সাধারণ, সস্তা<br><b>English:</b> Ordinary, inexpensive<br><b>Example:</b> Skilled workers aren't two a penny - they're valuable.	
Two Peas in A Pod	<b>Bengali:</b> দেখতে অনেক মিল আছে এমন দুজন<br><b>English:</b> Two people who are very similar in appearance<br><b>Example:</b> The sisters are like two peas in a pod.	
U Turn	<b>Bengali:</b> মতামত, দিক ইত্যাদির সম্পূর্ণ পরিবর্তন<br><b>English:</b> A complete change of opinion, direction, etc.<br><b>Example:</b> The politician made a U-turn on his tax policy.	
Ugly Duckling	<b>Bengali:</b> যে শিশু বা যুবক পরে সুন্দর হয়ে ওঠে<br><b>English:</b> An awkward child or young person who grows into a beautiful person<br><b>Example:</b> She was an ugly duckling in school but became a beautiful model.	
Under (Below) the Radar	<b>Bengali:</b> সাধারণভাবে অনুভূত নয়<br><b>English:</b> Not generally perceived, below popular consciousness<br><b>Example:</b> The company flew under the radar until their IPO.	
Under Someone's Spell	<b>Bengali:</b> কারো দ্বারা মুগ্ধ, বিমোহিত<br><b>English:</b> Fascinated, entranced by someone<br><b>Example:</b> The audience was under the magician's spell.	
Under the Impression	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু বিশ্বাস করা, হয়তো ভুলভাবে<br><b>English:</b> Believing something, perhaps mistakenly<br><b>Example:</b> I was under the impression that the meeting was cancelled.	
Under the Table	<b>Bengali:</b> আনুষ্ঠানিকভাবে লিপিবদ্ধ না করে<br><b>English:</b> Without being officially recorded<br><b>Example:</b> They paid him under the table to avoid taxes.	
Under the Weather	<b>Bengali:</b> অসুস্থ বোধ করা<br><b>English:</b> Feeling ill<br><b>Example:</b> I'm feeling under the weather today - I think I'll stay home.	
Under Wraps	<b>Bengali:</b> সাময়িকভাবে লুকানো, গোপন<br><b>English:</b> Temporarily hidden, secret<br><b>Example:</b> The new product is still under wraps.	
University of Life	<b>Bengali:</b> কঠিন বাস্তব জীবনের অভিজ্ঞতা<br><b>English:</b> Difficult real-life experience, as opposed to formal education<br><b>Example:</b> He didn't go to college - he graduated from the university of life.	
Until the Cows Come Home	<b>Bengali:</b> দীর্ঘ সময়ের জন্য<br><b>English:</b> For a long time<br><b>Example:</b> We could argue about this until the cows come home.	
Until You're Blue in the Face	<b>Bengali:</b> দীর্ঘ সময় ধরে ফলাফল ছাড়া<br><b>English:</b> For a long time with no results<br><b>Example:</b> You can complain until you're blue in the face, but nothing will change.	
Up a Creek	<b>Bengali:</b> খুব খারাপ পরিস্থিতিতে<br><b>English:</b> In a very bad situation<br><b>Example:</b> Without a car, we're really up a creek.	
Up for Grabs	<b>Bengali:</b> উপলব্ধ<br><b>English:</b> Available<br><b>Example:</b> The promotion is up for grabs - anyone can apply.	
Up in Arms	<b>Bengali:</b> রাগান্বিত, প্রতিবাদী<br><b>English:</b> Angry, protesting (usually said of a group)<br><b>Example:</b> The residents are up in arms about the new highway.	
Up in the Air	<b>Bengali:</b> এখনো সিদ্ধান্ত হয়নি<br><b>English:</b> Not yet decided<br><b>Example:</b> Our vacation plans are still up in the air.	
Up to One's Neck	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রায় অভিভূত<br><b>English:</b> Nearly overwhelmed<br><b>Example:</b> I'm up to my neck in work this week.	
Up to Scratch	<b>Bengali:</b> মৌলিক মান পূরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> Meeting a basic standard of competence or quality<br><b>Example:</b> Your work needs to be up to scratch for this project.	
Up to Snuff	<b>Bengali:</b> মৌলিক মান পূরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> Meeting a basic standard<br><b>Example:</b> The new employee's performance isn't up to snuff yet.	
Up the Ante	<b>Bengali:</b> ঝুঁকি বাড়ানো; গুরুত্ব বৃদ্ধি করা<br><b>English:</b> Raise the stakes; increase the importance of something under discussion<br><b>Example:</b> The company upped the ante by offering stock options.	
Up the Duff	<b>Bengali:</b> গর্ভবতী<br><b>English:</b> Pregnant<br><b>Example:</b> She's up the duff again - expecting her third child.	
Upset the Apple Cart	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু অগোছালো বা নষ্ট করা<br><b>English:</b> To disorganize or spoil something, especially an established arrangement or plan<br><b>Example:</b> Don't upset the apple cart by changing the schedule now.	
Use One's Head	<b>Bengali:</b> চিন্তা করা, সাধারণ জ্ঞান ব্যবহার করা<br><b>English:</b> To think, to have common sense<br><b>Example:</b> Use your head - that plan will never work.	
Vale of Tears	<b>Bengali:</b> জীবনের দুঃখ-কষ্ট<br><b>English:</b> The world in general, envisioned as a sad place; the tribulations of life<br><b>Example:</b> Life in this vale of tears can be difficult.	
Vicious Circle	<b>Bengali:</b> যে পরিস্থিতিতে সমস্যা সমাধানের চেষ্টা আরো সমস্যা তৈরি করে<br><b>English:</b> A situation in which an attempt to solve a problem makes the original problem worse<br><b>Example:</b> Poverty and lack of education create a vicious circle.	
Victory Lap	<b>Bengali:</b> বিজয়ের পর প্রকাশ্য উপস্থিতি<br><b>English:</b> Visible public appearances after a victory or accomplishment<br><b>Example:</b> After winning the election, she took a victory lap through the district.	
Virgin Territory	<b>Bengali:</b> যা কখনো অন্বেষণ করা হয়নি<br><b>English:</b> Something that has never been explored, physically or intellectually<br><b>Example:</b> This research area is virgin territory for scientists.	
Vote with One's Feet	<b>Bengali:</b> অসন্তুষ্টি প্রকাশের জন্য শারীরিকভাবে চলে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> To physically depart from something as a way of showing disapproval<br><b>Example:</b> When the company cut benefits, many employees voted with their feet.	
Waiting in the Wings	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রস্তুত অবস্থায় অপেক্ষা করা, উত্তরাধিকারী হওয়ার জন্য প্রস্তুত<br><b>English:</b> Ready to assume responsibilities but not yet active, ready to become a successor<br><b>Example:</b> The vice president is waiting in the wings for his chance to lead.	
Waka-Jumping	<b>Bengali:</b> রাজনৈতিক দল পরিবর্তন করা<br><b>English:</b> Change political parties (said of politicians themselves)<br><b>Example:</b> The senator's waka-jumping surprised everyone.	
Wake Up and Smell the Coffee	<b>Bengali:</b> নিজেকে ধোঁকা দেওয়া বন্ধ করো, বাস্তবতা বুঝো<br><b>English:</b> Stop deluding yourself<br><b>Example:</b> Wake up and smell the coffee - she's not interested in you.	
Wake Up on the Wrong Side of the Bed	<b>Bengali:</b> খিটখিটে বা খারাপ মেজাজে থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Be grumpy or ill-humored. Generally used in past tense<br><b>Example:</b> He woke up on the wrong side of the bed this morning.	
Walk on Eggshells	<b>Bengali:</b> কাউকে রাগান্বিত না করার জন্য অত্যন্ত সাবধানে আচরণ করা<br><b>English:</b> To have to act very sensitively in order to avoid offending someone<br><b>Example:</b> Everyone walks on eggshells around the temperamental boss.	
Walk the Plank	<b>Bengali:</b> পদত্যাগ করতে বাধ্য হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Be forced to resign a position<br><b>Example:</b> After the scandal, the CEO was forced to walk the plank.	
Wandering Eye	<b>Bengali:</b> প্রতিশ্রুতিবদ্ধ সঙ্গী ছাড়া অন্যদের প্রতি আকৃষ্ট হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> A tendency to look at and desire women or men other than one's committed romantic partner<br><b>Example:</b> His wandering eye got him in trouble with his wife.	
Wash Your Hands of (Something)	<b>Bengali:</b> দায়িত্ব নিতে অস্বীকার করা, আর জড়িত না থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Decline to take further responsibility; refuse to be involved with something anymore<br><b>Example:</b> I wash my hands of this whole mess.	
Water Under the Bridge	<b>Bengali:</b> অতীতের বিষয় যা নিয়ে আর চিন্তা করার দরকার নেই<br><b>English:</b> Something in the past that's no longer worth worrying about<br><b>Example:</b> Our old argument is water under the bridge now.	
Watering Hole	<b>Bengali:</b> মদের দোকান, বার<br><b>English:</b> A place where alcoholic beverages are served, a bar<br><b>Example:</b> Let's meet at the local watering hole after work.	
Weekend Warrior	<b>Bengali:</b> যে অফিসে কাজ করে কিন্তু সপ্তাহান্তে খেলাধুলা করে<br><b>English:</b> Someone who has an office job but enjoys contact sports on weekends; a member of a military reserve force<br><b>Example:</b> He's a weekend warrior who plays rugby every Saturday.	
We'll Cross That Bridge When We Come to It	<b>Bengali:</b> সমস্যা এলে তখন সমাধান করব<br><b>English:</b> We'll deal with that problem if and when it comes up<br><b>Example:</b> What if it rains? We'll cross that bridge when we come to it.	
Welsh (Welch) on a Deal	<b>Bengali:</b> চুক্তির শর্ত মানতে অস্বীকার করা<br><b>English:</b> Not observe the terms of an agreement<br><b>Example:</b> He welshed on the deal at the last minute.	
Wet Behind the Ears	<b>Bengali:</b> অনভিজ্ঞ, অপরিপক্ব, নতুন<br><b>English:</b> Inexperienced, immature, new to something<br><b>Example:</b> The new intern is still wet behind the ears.	
Wet Blanket	<b>Bengali:</b> যে উৎসবের আনন্দ নষ্ট করে<br><b>English:</b> Someone who dampens a festive occasion<br><b>Example:</b> Don't be such a wet blanket - join the party!	
Wet Your Whistle	<b>Bengali:</b> কিছু পান করা<br><b>English:</b> Drink something<br><b>Example:</b> Let's stop at the bar and wet our whistles.	
What Do You Make of (Him)?	<b>Bengali:</b> এই ব্যক্তি সম্পর্কে তোমার মতামত কী?<br><b>English:</b> What is your evaluation of this person?<br><b>Example:</b> What do you make of the new manager?	
What Goes Around Comes Around	<b>Bengali:</b> যেমন কর্ম তেমন ফল<br><b>English:</b> The kind of treatment you give to others will eventually return to you; things go in cycles<br><b>Example:</b> He treated his employees badly, and what goes around comes around.	
What's Good for the Goose Is Good for the Gander	<b>Bengali:</b> পুরুষের জন্য যা ঠিক, নারীর জন্যও তা ঠিক<br><b>English:</b> What's OK for a man is OK for a woman, too<br><b>Example:</b> If he can work late, so can she - what's good for the goose is good for the gander.	
When Hell Freezes Over	<b>Bengali:</b> কখনোই না<br><b>English:</b> Never<br><b>Example:</b> I'll forgive him when hell freezes over.	
When In Doubt, Leave It Out	<b>Bengali:</b> সন্দেহ থাকলে বাদ দিয়ে দাও<br><b>English:</b> When unsure about something, omit it<br><b>Example:</b> When in doubt about that quote, leave it out of your speech.	
When in Rome, Do as the Romans Do	<b>Bengali:</b> যেখানে যাও সেখানকার রীতি মানো<br><b>English:</b> When you visit a new place, follow the customs of the people there<br><b>Example:</b> I don't usually eat with my hands, but when in Rome, do as the Romans do.	
When It Rains, It Pours	<b>Bengali:</b> বিপদ একা আসে না<br><b>English:</b> Problems tend to come in groups<br><b>Example:</b> First my car broke down, then I got sick - when it rains, it pours.	
When Pigs Fly	<b>Bengali:</b> কখনোই না<br><b>English:</b> Never<br><b>Example:</b> He'll clean his room when pigs fly.	
When the Chips Are Down	<b>Bengali:</b> যখন পরিস্থিতি কঠিন হয়ে ওঠে<br><b>English:</b> When a situation becomes urgent or difficult<br><b>Example:</b> When the chips are down, she always comes through.	
Where (When) the Rubber Meets the Road	<b>Bengali:</b> বাস্তবে; যেখানে ধারণা বাস্তব পরীক্ষার মুখোমুখি হয়<br><b>English:</b> In reality; where an idea meets a real-world test<br><b>Example:</b> The theory sounds good, but where the rubber meets the road, it doesn't work.	
Where There's a Will, There's a Way	<b>Bengali:</b> যেখানে ইচ্ছা সেখানে উপায়<br><b>English:</b> If you have a strong desire to accomplish something, you will achieve it even in the face of considerable odds<br><b>Example:</b> She was determined to finish college, and where there's a will, there's a way.	
Where There's Smoke, There's Fire	<b>Bengali:</b> ধোঁয়া দেখলে আগুন আছে বুঝতে হবে<br><b>English:</b> If there is typical evidence of something, the most likely explanation is that it is actually occurring<br><b>Example:</b> Where there's smoke, there's fire - those rumors might be true.	
Whisper Sweet Nothings (in Someone's Ear)	<b>Bengali:</b> কানে কানে প্রেমের কথা বলা<br><b>English:</b> Speak meaningless romantic utterances<br><b>Example:</b> The couple was whispering sweet nothings to each other.	
Whistle in the Dark	<b>Bengali:</b> অজ্ঞতায় সাহসী ভান করা<br><b>English:</b> To be unrealistically confident or brave; to talk about something of which one has little knowledge<br><b>Example:</b> His confident predictions are just whistling in the dark.	
Whistle Past the Graveyard	<b>Bengali:</b> বিপদ থাকা সত্ত্বেও আশাবাদী থাকা<br><b>English:</b> Remain optimistic despite dangers; be clueless<br><b>Example:</b> Ignoring the financial crisis is like whistling past the graveyard.	
Whistling Dixie	<b>Bengali:</b> অবাস্তব আশাবাদী হওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Being unrealistically optimistic<br><b>Example:</b> If you think the project will finish on time, you're whistling Dixie.	
White Elephant	<b>Bengali:</b> অপ্রয়োজনীয় বোঝা<br><b>English:</b> An unwanted item that is difficult to sell or dispose of<br><b>Example:</b> That expensive equipment turned out to be a white elephant.	
Who's She, the Cat's Mother?	<b>Bengali:</b> সে নিজেকে কী মনে করে?<br><b>English:</b> Why does she have such a high opinion of herself?<br><b>Example:</b> She wants special treatment? Who's she, the cat's mother?	
Wild Goose Chase	<b>Bengali:</b> অসম্ভব বা নিষ্ফল অনুসন্ধান<br><b>English:</b> An impossible or futile search or task<br><b>Example:</b> Looking for that lost earring was a wild goose chase.	
Window Dressing	<b>Bengali:</b> ভাল ছাপ দেওয়ার জন্য ছদ্মবেশ<br><b>English:</b> A misleading disguise intended to present a favorable impression<br><b>Example:</b> The company's diversity program is just window dressing.	
Window Shop	<b>Bengali:</b> কেনার ইচ্ছা ছাড়াই দোকানের জিনিস দেখা<br><b>English:</b> To look at merchandise in a store without intending to buy it<br><b>Example:</b> We spent the afternoon window shopping downtown.	
Witch Hunt	<b>Bengali:</b> অনিষ্ট করার জন্য কারো বিরুদ্ধে সংগঠিত প্রচেষ্টা<br><b>English:</b> An organized attempt to persecute an unpopular group of people and blame them for a problem<br><b>Example:</b> The investigation turned into a witch hunt against innocent employees.	
With Bells On	<b>Bengali:</b> উৎসাহের সাথে, স্বেচ্ছায় এবং সময়মতো<br><b>English:</b> Eagerly, willingly, and on time<br><b>Example:</b> I'll be at your party with bells on!	
Work One's Fingers to the Bone	<b>Bengali:</b> অত্যন্ত কঠোর পরিশ্রম করা<br><b>English:</b> Work very hard over an extended period<br><b>Example:</b> She worked her fingers to the bone to support her family.	
Worn to a Frazzle	<b>Bengali:</b> সম্পূর্ণ ক্লান্ত, শেষ হয়ে যাওয়া<br><b>English:</b> Exhausted, completely worn out<br><b>Example:</b> After the long conference, I was worn to a frazzle.	
Wouldn't Be Caught Dead	<b>Bengali:</b> এটা কখনোই করব না<br><b>English:</b> Would absolutely not allow myself to do this<br><b>Example:</b> I wouldn't be caught dead wearing that outfit.
